taxon:Root
  D "Temporary ontology terms for NCBI Protein GI"
bae:BAE_0000020
  D "Serum is the blood fraction remaining after the natural coagulation of blood, followed by centrifugation to remove any remaining red blood cells. Serum is thought to provide basic elements required for cell culture, including growth factors, attachment factors, iron transporters, vitamins, amino acids, lipids, carbohydrates, hormones, and trace elements. Fetal bovine serum (FBS), also called fetal calf serum (FCS), comes from the blood drawn from a bovine (cow) fetus via a closed system of collection at the slaughterhouse. FBS/FCS is the most widely used serum-supplement for the in vitro cell culture of eukaryotic cells. This is due to it having a very low level of antibodies and containing more growth factors, allowing for versatility in many different cell culture applications. Serum contains many factors that are not controlled for, which can have a direct or indirect effect on the cells in culture, thus creating significant variability between suppliers and lots from a single supplier. Different methods, such as heat inactivation or dialysis, are sometimes used to eliminate undesired components (such as labile growth factors, vitamins, etc. or the complement system). Some suppliers test serum for the presence of other factors such as tetracylcine or mycoplasma."
